Page 9

閻錫山擬訂之 土地公有大綱 以土地公有為防共政策 防共會議决定要案多項

Taiyuan Correspondent: The Jin Province authorities have recently been increasingly concerned about the rampant communist bandits in northern Shaanxi. As Jin and Shaanxi are closely connected, preventive measures cannot be ignored. Pacification Director Yan Xishan, in addition to dispatching troops to cooperate in suppressing the Shaanxi bandits, also plans to take other political measures for thorough prevention. Therefore, he summoned the magistrates of 21 counties along the river and near the bandit areas in western Shanxi to the provincial capital to jointly hold a conference on preventing communism at the Pacification Headquarters, along with the heads of various responsible agencies. The conference lasted for more than ten days and has now concluded. During the conference, detailed discussions were held on various measures to prevent communism. The plan to transfer land ownership to the village public and implement the old well-field system to ensure that tillers have land is the central issue among various proposals. On the morning of the 16th, during the joint weekly memorial service of the Pacification and Provincial Headquarters, he made a public and concrete report on the various measures he proposed and the various proposals discussed at the conference on preventing communism. The report is summarized as follows:

防共會議 議决案件

Yan's report stated, "The communist party in northern Shaanxi is currently rampant, and the defense of western Shanxi is strained. In order to devise appropriate measures to prevent communism, I convened a meeting of the magistrates of 21 counties along the river. The meetings were held every afternoon from August 29th to September 11th, totaling 14 days. The discussions covered 35 items, which can be broadly divided into two categories. The first category is fundamental measures to prevent communism, which is to transfer land ownership to the village. The second category is effective measures to prevent communism at present, which include: (1) Handling the case of the anti-communist defense corps; (2) Eliminating popular grievances; (3) Promoting and reorganizing new people's factories in various counties; (4) Stipulating measures to restrict usury by political power; (5) Requiring elementary school teachers in various counties to be responsible for propaganda and assist in preventing communism; (6) Managing the method of tenant farming; (7) Educating the wealthy, workers, and vagrants; (8) Radically reforming apathetic politics and strictly defining punitive measures; (9) Distributing work to the people to reduce unemployment and implementing village governance and rural construction; (10) Reorganizing police affairs; (11) Clearing arrears of police salaries; (12) Implementing joint office work in the provincial government and changing bureaus to sections in county governments; (13) Addressing the difficulty of the county magistrate concurrently serving as the head of the first district; (14) Defining the method for counties along the river to purchase supplies for the stationed troops on behalf of the province; (15) Defining the method for counties to send suspected communist bandits captured to the province; (16) Defining how to deal with goods seized that are used to supply bandit areas; (17) Repairing the highway from Hegu to Sancha; (18) Addressing the shortage of judicial funds in various counties and how to plan them uniformly; (19) Banning private boats south of Hejin and including Ronghe in the defense zone for blocking passage; (20) Government agencies should keep the names of informants confidential when handling public affairs; (21) Roads in the bandit suppression area should be repaired by stationed troops and civilian laborers, and a method for exempting grain should be defined for occupied civilian land; (22) The provincial government should subsidize or lend electrical materials for the installation of telephones at key passes in various districts and cards; (23) Punishments for truancy and desertion by anti-communist defense corps members should be stipulated; (24) How to handle urgent financial needs during the anti-communist period; (25) Setting the position of village chief as a paid position with an annual vehicle and horse allowance of 570 yuan to reward and encourage specialized responsibility; (26) Building bunkers at key passes along the river when necessary; (27) Planning centralized housing for scattered villages along the river when necessary; (28) Whether the travel expenses required for counties to send personnel to rural areas to handle anti-communist defense corps affairs can be paid from local funds; (29) Whether the anti-communist defense corps and various defense police in the 21 counties along the river should be handled in conjunction with the anti-communist defense corps; (30) How the county government agencies should handle cases where there are no funds to cover the costs of anti-communist defense corps clothing and establishment; (31) How the anti-communist responsibilities of county magistrates, stationed troops, and the anti-communist defense corps should be divided; (32) Joint defense measures for counties within the anti-communist zone; (33) Organizing a good people's group to punish bad people; (34) Stipulating a reasonable method for counties and villages to bear financial burdens." These second-category cases are originally within the regular scope of politics and should have been handled long ago. It was not until the communists came to pressure us that we started to handle them. In particular, the matter of punishing the families and relatives of civil and military officials and gentry who bully the people has only been done now for the people, which is truly too shameful to face the people. I feel very ashamed and wish that my colleagues would also feel ashamed, not procrastinate and neglect, and not underestimate the grievances of the people. I hope that all public officials will restrain their families and relatives. I have personally instructed the county magistrates to break through feelings and advocate fairness from now on. If there are relatives of officials and gentry who bully others by relying on their power, they should be dealt with impartially. Anyone who protects them will be punished for dereliction of duty. As for the first-category fundamental measures to prevent communism by making land public to the village, this is not the regular practice of current laws and regulations, and it should be submitted to the central government for approval before it can be implemented. The outline of the land public ownership plan is as follows:

土地公有 辦法大綱

(1) The village public office will issue interest-free public bonds to purchase all the land in the village and make it publicly owned by the village. (2) According to the water, drought, fertility, and barrenness of the land, it will be divided into several portions, with the amount that one person can cultivate as one portion, and distributed to farmers with village registration for cultivation. (3) If the villagers' meeting decides to cultivate the land in the village jointly, it will be designated as a joint farm. (4) If the land is not sufficient for the farmers in the village to cultivate, the village public office should find other work for those who have not obtained land. If there is surplus land that cannot be cultivated, the surplus land should be reported to the county government for immigrants to cultivate, in order to provide land for landless cultivators in other villages. (5) The age of farmers for cultivation is set at 18 to 58 years old. People who are 18 years old have the right to apply to the village public office for land. At the age of 58, the originally received land should be returned to the village public office. (6) If a farmer has any of the following circumstances, the village public office should take back the land received: 1. Death; 2. Change of occupation; 3. Abandonment of cultivation; 4. Migration; 5. Criminal conviction. When the land is taken back, compensation should be given for the effective improvement work on the land. (7) The land cultivated by farmers during the period of military service should be cultivated on average by the farmers in the village on their behalf. (8) If a farmer's cultivation ability declines, or the land requires meticulous work, or special crops that require labor are planted, they should be allowed to use hired labor, but the hired labor is limited to the following three types: A. Other farmers who have free time and spare capacity; B. Men who are under 18 years old and over 58 years old; C. Women within the laboring age. (9) At the beginning of implementation, farmers' burdens on the province, county, and local areas will still be collected as before. (10) The guarantee for the annual repayment of the principal of the public bonds for land purchase is as follows: A. Property protection tax: 1% of all movable and immovable property will be drawn annually as a property protection tax; B. Non-labor tax: Villagers who do not work without legitimate reasons should be levied a non-labor tax in accordance with the average labor income tax paid by a farmer for one portion of land; C. Income tax on capital interest: Those who earn interest from capital should be levied a progressive income tax based on 30% of the income; D. Labor income tax: Those who have income from labor should levy labor income tax according to the following standards: 1. Cultivation of land income: 10% will be taken; 2. Income from labor other than cultivation: A progressive income tax based on 1% will be levied. (11) Grave land and house sites will not be purchased for the time being. After the land is purchased and owned by the village, if the buyer is old, weak, and has no labor capacity, and has no one to support them, and the amount of public bonds they should receive each year is not enough to support their livelihood, the village should separately establish support measures, supporting the old until death and the young until adulthood. (12) Public land such as village mountain forests, ponds, and pastures will be acquired in accordance with land purchase procedures, except for those owned by the state, province, county, and village. Compensation should be given for the valuable items on the land. (13) The village public office should redistribute the land appropriately according to the increase in population and the state of land improvement. (Explanation) Solving the land problem is not a small matter, nor is it an easy one. However, purchasing it with village public bonds and managing it by the village itself is not such a difficult task. Matters have their difficulties and ease. If handled properly, difficult matters can be easily handled. If not handled properly, easy matters can be difficult. Moreover, the need for things should not be determined by their difficulty. Today's private land ownership is a big loophole for the communist party and an explosive that is buried in the current society. Public land ownership has become an inevitable trend. Some people think that the communist party in Jiangxi expanded because it failed to solve the land problem. That is true, but the communist party in Jiangxi exhausted the country's strength and took several years to merely destroy it. The rural areas in the northwest are bankrupt, with ten households and nine poverty-stricken, and the land is vast and the troops are scattered, making it difficult to blockade. The spread of the red disaster seems impossible to prevent with this small force. Without starting from solving the land problem and fundamentally eliminating the big loophole, I am afraid there is no other way. However, this matter is significant, and there were several questions raised in the meeting. Here are excerpts: (To be continued)

王克敏 離平晉京情況 過津時訪問多田 擬謁汪後往訪黃

Beiping Correspondent: The files and documents of the Beiping Political Affairs Readjustment Committee were handed over on the 16th of this month. Important documents were packed under the supervision of Huang Qiuyue, Secretary of the Executive Yuan, and are scheduled to be escorted back to Nanjing tomorrow (20th). All valuable items of the committee, such as automobiles, are also being handled for transportation by Wang Yizhi, Secretary of the Executive Yuan. It is expected that they can be shipped south on the (21st). Xu Xiuzhi, the internal representative responsible for the takeover, left Beiping at 8:45 this morning (19th) with the seal of the Political Affairs Committee. As he had important matters to discuss with Cheng Ke, the mayor of Tianjin, Xu would stay in Tianjin for several hours and then take a train south to report to Nanjing.

Wang Kemin, the acting chairman of the committee, decided to go to Nanjing tomorrow (20th) because he had repeatedly received telegrams from Premier Wang of the Executive Yuan. However, since Tada Shun, the commander of the Japanese troops stationed in Tianjin, had come to Beiping last time to pay a courtesy visit upon taking office, Wang had not yet returned the visit. Therefore, Wang first went to Tianjin tonight (19th) and is scheduled to visit Tada at the residence of a Japanese officer in Zhangguo tomorrow (20th) to thank him for his previous visit to Beiping. He will then take a train on the Pingpu Line to Nanjing that evening. According to Wang, when speaking to reporters at the station before his departure, "The Political Affairs Committee has been completely concluded, and the files, except for confidential documents taken to Nanjing, have been placed in the archives custody department. I will stay in Tianjin for one night, and after returning the visit to Commander Tada of the Japanese army tomorrow (20th), I will go to Nanjing that evening to report everything. Then I will go to Moganshan to visit Minister Huang (Fu) to make a similar report. I will return to the north half a month later to take care of the funeral of my family members."

Someone asked Wang about (1) the recent situation of the Hua Zuozhou case, (2) Song Zheyuan's delay in coming to Beiping, and (3) the survival or abolition of the Tianjin-Gu Security Command. According to Wang's answer, the main culprit in the Liu case is still under interrogation, and it has not yet been decided when to bring him back to Tangshan for re-examination. Commander Song's assumption of office is not far away and he can come to Beiping soon. The Tianjin-Gu Security Command will not be revoked for the time being. Wang then talked about the Committee for the Reorganization of Cultural Relics in the Old Capital, saying that the only vacancies in the committee are the members and chairman of the former Political Affairs Readjustment Committee. How to supplement them will be discussed at a meeting of the Executive Yuan. The members of the Ministries of Education, Railways, Finance, and Internal Affairs remain unchanged. The reporter then asked Wang about the recent situation of the Hebei Economic Association. Wang replied that the organizational charter has been drafted and it is rumored that the inaugural meeting will be held tomorrow (20th). At this point, the train had already whistled, and Wang was helped onto the train by someone and left Beiping. Those traveling with him included his fifth wife, his daughter, and Secretary Wang, totaling more than ten people.

Those who came to the station to see him off included heads of various military and political agencies and Shang Zhan, Chairman of the Hebei Provincial Government, creating a fairly warm scene. Before Wang Kemin's departure, key members of the former Political Affairs Readjustment Committee, including He Qiqun, Yu Jiaqi, Zhou Yongneng, Gan Yuli, Bao Junjian, and Zhang Jianchu, went to Fengzeyuan to attend the farewell banquet hosted by Yin Rugeng, Commissioner of the Luan Yu District. Except for He Qiqun, Gan Yuli, and Bao Junjian, who will remain in Beiping, the others will leave Beiping for the south at 6:50 pm tomorrow (20th). They raised funds to purchase a chartered carriage for their use. The carriage has already been parked on the platform, loading boxes and other items. Yin Rugeng arrived in Beiping from Tianjin at 5:50 pm today (19th). Because Wang will pay a courtesy visit to Tada tomorrow (20th), he is scheduled to take a plane to Tianjin at 5 am tomorrow (20th) to attend the meeting.

Fresh Pork Vendors Association Requests Strict Prohibition of Live Plucking of Pig Bristles 27

Workers in the pig consignment stores and barge rooms of Xuejia浜 in the South City often start plucking pig bristles after autumn, when the bristles begin to grow. After the piglets are injured, they either refuse to eat, lose weight, or die suddenly, resulting in confiscation by the health bureau. The losses over the years have been substantial. To prevent this, the Shanghai Fresh Pork Vendors Association sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, requesting them to consult with the Public Security Bureau to strictly prohibit and investigate this practice. They also sent a letter to the Fresh Pork Industry Association, urging them to effectively improve management methods to benefit vendors. The two letters are excerpted below:

Letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce:

Respectfully, every autumn, pig bristles gradually grow. The piglets transported to Shanghai for sale must first be delivered to the consignment stores via pig barges. The workers in the pig consignment stores and barge rooms of Xuejia浜 in the South City seek their own profit by wantonly plucking pig bristles while the piglets are being transported on the Huangpu River. After the piglets are stored in the consignment stores, the workers pluck the bristles a second time, removing them almost entirely, causing bleeding and leaving wounds all over the body. The piglets cry out in agony. After being injured, the piglets may refuse to eat, lose weight, and become injured pigs, or they may suddenly become ill and die. The industry suffers unexpected losses and heavy financial damage. Although the association previously obtained approval from the Social, Public Security, and Health Bureaus to issue a strict prohibition notice, the uneducated workers have become lax over time, driven by greed, disregarding the law, and continuing to pluck bristles as before. Therefore, we respectfully request your esteemed chamber to promptly consult with the Public Security Bureau and instruct the water patrol and relevant branch bureaus to strictly prohibit and investigate this practice. Any workers found plucking pig bristles and those purchasing raw bristles should be arrested and prosecuted to prevent the spread of this harmful practice and benefit the industry. We would be deeply grateful.

Letter to the Fresh Pork Industry Association:

Regarding the practice of live plucking of pig bristles, it is inhumane, and the authorities have repeatedly issued strict prohibitions. The piglets transported by our industry for sale to your industry are delivered from the Huangpu River to the consignment stores, with a barging fee of five cents per head and a storage fee of four cents after storage. The workers are employed by your industry's consignment stores and should be protected. Currently, during autumn, when pig bristles gradually grow, the piglets brought to the South City by our industry are often subjected to live plucking by barge and consignment store workers, resulting in significant losses. As a result, Shanghai has become a fearful destination. This indirectly affects the future of your industry. As closely related and interdependent parties, if no measures are taken to prohibit this practice soon, the losses suffered by both parties will be immeasurable in the future. Moreover, the pig consignment stores in the Wusong and Yangjing districts of this city have been in operation for many years and have been able to effectively restrain their workers, with no reports of bristle plucking. The pig consignment stores in the South City are also under the leadership of your association and should not be treated differently. Therefore, to avoid disputes, we respectfully request your esteemed association to investigate and take responsibility for improving management and warning workers. Implement the instructions of the Municipal Party Headquarters, and if any workers are found plucking pig bristles, they should be immediately dismissed from their jobs as a warning to others, to prevent the spread of this harmful practice, benefit both parties, and protect livestock. We would be deeply grateful.

Small Owner of Huizhong Hotel Accused of Abandonment and Breach of Trust: Ten Years of Affection Down the Drain, No Regard for Living Expenses 28

Sun Zhongyi, a native of Changshu, resides at No. 46, Lane 1124, Xinzha Road, and is the junior owner of the old Huizhong Hotel in Maijiaquan. He owns considerable real estate in Shanghai. Ten years ago, Sun met Wang Yuying, a local woman, through a friend's introduction. Wang Yuying comes from a distinguished family, possesses a beautiful appearance, and has a good command of Chinese and Western languages. She is currently 28 years old. After meeting Sun Zhongyi, their relationship became harmonious, and friendship developed into love. Sun then kept her in a golden house and began living together. In addition to Sun covering all expenses, he also provided Wang Yuying with an additional 100 yuan per month for personal use. Two years ago, Sun and Wang Yuying had a quarrel over a minor matter, and Sun physically assaulted Wang Yuying. The two became irreconcilable. Later, Wang hired a lawyer to negotiate with Sun, and friends mediated the dispute. Sun paid Wang Yuying 10,000 yuan in cash and issued several promissory notes totaling 40,000 yuan as Wang Yuying's future living expenses. The matter was temporarily resolved. Unexpectedly, three days ago, Sun's promissory notes gradually matured, but Sun's feelings for Wang Yuying were quite restored. Therefore, on March 21st of last year, lawyer Yao Yongli acted on behalf of both parties to draw up a cohabitation agreement, stipulating that Sun Zhongyi would bear all expenses and pay Wang Yuying a monthly allowance, and they should live together in love and harmony until old age. At the same time, Wang Yuying believed that since she was cohabitating with Sun, she would not be as unprotected as before, so she agreed to Sun's request and handed over all the matured promissory notes for 40,000 yuan in living expenses to Sun through lawyer Yao. Unexpectedly, not long after, Sun suddenly went back on his word, disappeared from Wang Yuying's residence, and did not provide for her living expenses, effectively abandoning her. Wang Yuying was forced to hire lawyer Zhang Li to file a complaint with the Criminal Division of the First Special Court, accusing Sun Zhongyi of abandonment and fraud, violating Article 294, Section 1, and Article 339 of the Criminal Law. She requested that the court summon and investigate the case and filed a private lawsuit, requesting that the defendant be ordered to return the 40,000 yuan in living expenses and 4,300 yuan in pawned jewelry. At 11:00 AM yesterday, Liu Yugui, a prosecutor from the Special Court, received Wang Yuying's complaint, stating that she was 28 years old, currently residing at her mother's home at No. 26, Bugaofang, Avenue Albert, and had known the defendant for ten years but had not married him. Zhang Li, the plaintiff's lawyer, stated that the defendant owned thousands of acres of good land and considerable real estate. Due to previous debts, his residence on Xinzha Road was sealed. Now, his whereabouts are unknown, and a warrant should be issued for his arrest. Prosecutor Liu adjourned the case to the afternoon of the 28th of this month, pending the defendant's arrival for further questioning.

Crime Statistics for August in the Public Concession 29

According to the Public Works Bureau Police Department's report for August, a total of 1,422 reported criminal cases were recorded for the month, an increase of 29 cases compared to July and an increase of 34 cases compared to the same month last year. The number of criminals arrested this month also increased compared to the previous months, with a total of 1,374 arrests. In addition, 105 individuals who committed crimes in previous months were apprehended in August, and 100 individuals were arrested on behalf of other local authorities. By type of crime, one murder case and one attempted murder case were reported in August. There were 19 robbery cases this month, a decrease of 8 cases compared to July but an increase of 9 cases compared to the same month last year. There were 16 ordinary theft cases, 37 residential burglary cases, and 30 residential robbery cases. In addition, Group A reports for August included 12 shop robbery cases, a decrease of 7 cases compared to the previous month, with 15 bandits apprehended. There were 103 pickpocketing cases, an increase of 6 cases compared to the previous month, with 82 pickpockets apprehended. Stolen vehicles included 4 automobiles and 47 bicycles. All 4 automobiles were recovered, one with missing parts, and 10 bicycles were recovered. A total of 15 thieves were arrested. Furthermore, there were 34 snatching cases, with 40 criminals apprehended. In August, the total reported value of property lost to theft was 262,876 yuan, while the value of recovered property reached 286,022 yuan. In August, there were 14 male suicides, 9 female suicides, and 1 foreign male suicide in the concession.

Ministry of Finance Approves: No Stamp Duty Required for Bus Tickets 30

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Taxi Industry Association yesterday, stating that no stamp duty is required for taxi tickets. The original letter stated: "Respectfully, regarding your previous letter inquiring whether taxi tickets could be exempt from stamp duty, we submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance and replied to you earlier. On the 18th of this month, we received the Ministry's approval letter No. 7152, stating: 'Having received your telegram, after investigation, taxi tickets are a type of ticket and should be included within the scope of 'tickets' as mentioned in Article 3, Section 10 of the Stamp Tax Law and can be exempt from stamp duty. Please inform and comply accordingly.' Respectfully, we are forwarding the approval for your information and compliance."

Opposing Hidden Surcharges on Transport Fees: Fresh Meat Industry Submits to Municipal Party Headquarters Again, Requesting Orders for Companies to Reduce Slaughter Fees 36

More than 1,000 fresh meat industries in the Public Concession oppose the hidden surcharges on transport fees by the Ninghai, Ninghu, Suzhou, and Xiren slaughter companies. Yesterday, they submitted a report to the Municipal Party Headquarters again, requesting that the four companies be ordered to reduce slaughter fees and to publish the accounts and organizational content of previous years. The original report stated: "Submitting a request for approval to order the Ninghu, Ninghai, Suzhou, and Xiren slaughter companies to reduce industry fees and to publish the accounts and organizational content of previous years to reduce the burden on the industry and clarify the truth. Your honor, our industries have been affected by the hidden surcharges on transport fees by the Ninghu, Ninghai, Suzhou, and Xiren slaughter companies and are experiencing great difficulties in operation. Therefore, we previously submitted a request to your esteemed association to stop it in accordance with the law. Your esteemed association summoned both parties for mediation on the 7th of the month. As a result, the four companies denied the hidden national transport fees, claiming that they only recognized management fees and entry fees. The four companies are not only inconsistent and contradictory in their statements, but also the transport fees and all fees paid by our industries over the years have been paid by the pig consignment stores. There is no allowance for company management fees on the consignment notes (verifiable). Even if there is, how can it be paid by the freight company? This is an obvious fact, which shows that their hidden surcharges on transport fees have been fully revealed. The four companies are cooperative businesses of our industries and should protect the interests of the industries. However, they are doing the opposite, ignoring the suffering of the industries, exploiting them, and increasing the burden on the industries. Moreover, since the establishment of the companies, they have had surpluses every year. The accounts and all organizational content have never been clearly published, which has obscured the industries and made them unable to understand the details. All kinds of shady scenes have been clearly identified. At the same time, a general meeting of all industries has not been held, or the board of directors has been re-elected. A few people have taken control and are running rampant, regarding the company as their own, which is extremely illegal. The companies and our industries are cooperative businesses, and their interests are closely related. One point of surplus for the four companies is one point of loss for our industries. In the current economic downturn and soaring freight prices, if remedial measures are not taken urgently, the future of the industries is unimaginable. In order to seek the survival of the industries, the entire industry meeting decided to jointly submit a request to your esteemed association to order the four companies to reduce industry fees as much as possible, excluding the offset of income and expenses, as long as they can maintain them (that is, slaughter fees, also known as company tickets). Publish the accounts and organizational content of previous years to reduce the burden and show great trust. Also, the previous request to stop the companies from secretly increasing transport fees should be considered together. When submitting, I am overwhelmed with the urgency of waiting for orders. Respectfully submitted to the Executive Committee of the Shanghai Special City Party Department, Lu Gaojian and more than 1,000 fresh meat industries."

They first held the men and women in the house under surveillance and then forced them to hand over the keys to the chests. They ransacked the house and looted all valuables. The police chief dispatched detectives to investigate and carefully list the losses, which were reported to be considerable.

Lawyer Jin Hongji Acquitted of Fraud Charges, Incidental Civil Suit Dismissed 45

Jin Hongji (also known as Jin Youmei), a native of the county residing at No. 24 Wengjia Lane, Ximennei, has been practicing law in Shanghai since 1920. Recently, he purchased a 7 mu, 7 fen, 5 li, 1 hao piece of land with deed number 1197 and a 5 fen, 6 li, 1 hao piece of land on Turas脱 Road in the French Concession, behind the Shanghai Funeral Home, worth approximately 400,000 yuan. He mortgaged it to Huaan Insurance Company for 200,000 yuan and built Fuli New Village洋房 on the land. A mortgage construction contract was signed, stipulating that the rent collected after the completion of the houses would be used for interest payments. If there was a surplus, 500 yuan would be given each month. On January 6th of this year, through the introduction of Zhang Zhiliang of Xinshengji Construction Factory on Songshan Road, he borrowed 5,000 yuan from Jing Tiansheng, a native of Shaoxing residing at No. 170 West Ames Road, with a six-month term for redemption at any time. Clause 6 of the Huaan Company's mortgage construction contract, which stipulates that the monthly interest of 500 yuan would be used as security, was also used as collateral, and it was noted that if the contract was breached upon maturity, Jing Tiansheng would directly collect the monthly payment of 500 yuan from Huaan Company. Later, due to the economic downturn, the loan could not be repaid upon maturity. The creditor sent a letter to Huaan Company asserting his rights. He was informed that Jin Youmei had mortgaged the property for the second time in April of the previous year for 24,000 yuan, using the first mortgaged property as secondary collateral. Jing Tiansheng believed that Jin Youmei had not disclosed the second mortgage to Huaan at the time of the loan, which was considered fraudulent. He hired lawyers Ma Junshuo and Xu Jingqing to file a self-prosecution lawsuit for fraud in the Criminal Division of the Second Court, based on Article 339, Section 1 of the Criminal Law, and filed a civil suit to recover the loan principal and interest. The court accepted the case, and on the morning of the 17th, Judge Qiu Huanqi summoned the defendant, who hired lawyer Chen Yun to defend him. After questioning the facts in court, the lawyers were ordered to debate, and a date was set for sentencing. The details of this case were published in the newspaper on the 18th. The sentencing date was yesterday morning. The plaintiff and his lawyer did not appear, and only the defendant's lawyer, Chen Yun, appeared to wait for instructions. Judge Qiu and Secretary Zhang Guancheng ascended to the Criminal Court No. 2 and announced the verdict. The main text was that Jin Youmei was not guilty, and the incidental civil suit of the plaintiff was dismissed.

Japanese merchants bought Indian cotton in large quantities, and futures traders also bought, but this was offset by long positions and cross-selling by some European exporters. The prices of both Ping Guo Er and Oom Lah rose by one rupee, and White Luo Creek rose by 0.75 rupee. The original telegram is recorded on the left. (Telegraph on the 19th)

According to the Bombay telegram, the opening forecast for White Luo Creek cotton on the 20th was 200 rupees, up three-quarters of a rupee compared to the previous day's close. Food Prices, Impact of the serious European situation, wheat prices rise sharply.

The flour market rose sharply again. The price of foreign wheat was reported, with Chicago rising 7 jiao and Canada rising 7-8 jiao. With maritime war risk insurance rising sharply, overseas wheat markets also rose due to the East African incident. After the opening price, there was an increase of 2-3 fen, and then both industry insiders and outsiders bought aggressively, and the sellers could not meet the demand, further increasing by 3-4 fen. It is estimated that the transaction for half a day reached more than 800,000 bags, which shows the deterioration of the situation. By the time the market opened in the afternoon, individual investors had been released, and no major investors were absorbing them in the market. The trend was relatively moderate, and transactions were also slightly less. It is estimated that more than 500,000 bags were transacted. The key to the rise and fall is entirely in the international wheat market, so there is little accurate speculation.

Egyptian Government Increases Import Tax on Japanese Goods; Japanese Foreign Ministry Plans to Protest 53

Cairo - Official sources claim that, effective today, all pure cotton or rayon fabrics from Japan, as well as fabrics containing 50% or more cotton or rayon, will be subject to an additional surcharge of 440% on the assessed value, in addition to the regular tax, to compensate for exchange rate fluctuations. (Reuters, 20th)

Cairo - According to today's announcement, effective tomorrow, import tariffs on Japanese cotton goods will be increased by 40%. According to current tariffs, taxes range from 25 to 160 milliemes per kilogram. (Reuters, 19th)

(Tokyo) The Japanese Consul-General in Alexandria has reported to the Foreign Ministry regarding the Egyptian government's increase in tariffs on Japanese cotton cloth. The Japanese government, in order to adjust the overall situation of Japanese-Egyptian trade, has dispatched a negotiating representative, Mr. Kasama Kayao, to Egypt. However, expressing regret over the uncompromising attitude of the Egyptian government, the Commerce Bureau immediately discussed countermeasures. As a result, believing that this violates the most-favored-nation clause, they have decided to issue a serious protest to urge the Egyptian government to reconsider. (Japanese United News, 20th)

Emperor as an Organ Theory Issue: Military Takes a Strong Stance, Potential Political Upheaval 54

(Tokyo) Within the Navy Ministry, due to Dr. Minobe's statement not admitting the errors in his writings, the attitude has hardened. Prior to today's cabinet meeting, Navy Minister Osumi met with Justice Minister Ohara and Prime Minister Okada to investigate the Ministry of Justice's decision not to prosecute. After questioning the Prime Minister's beliefs, he then consulted with Army Minister Kawashima and decided that the Army and Navy would jointly issue a serious warning to the government. (Dentsu News, 20th)

(Tokyo) The government believed that this incident had come to an end after the Ministry of Justice decided on Dr. Minobe's punishment, and was optimistic about the future. However, the facts are not so. As soon as the military expressed opposition to the punishment, the so-called Emperor as an Organ Theory issue reignited. There are disagreements between the government and the military, and between the judicial authorities and the military. The consequences of this have a significant impact on the political world. Those seeking to overthrow the cabinet are seizing the opportunity of the military's strong stance to actively carry out the work of overthrowing the cabinet. The fate of the Okada Cabinet is not optimistic. (Japanese United News, 20th)

US President Appoints Financial and Legal Advisors to the Philippines 55

(Washington) The office of the United States High Commissioner to Manila will establish two positions: a legal advisor and a financial advisor. President Roosevelt today appointed Compton as legal advisor and Jones as financial advisor. The Philippine Commonwealth government will be formally established in November, and the two advisors will assist the High Commissioner in his work. (National Telegram, 19th)

Lithuania Prepares to Protest Hitler's Remarks; Lithuanian Foreign Minister Meets with Laval 56

(Paris) According to a dispatch from Memel, the Lithuanian government has decided to jointly protest to Hitler with France, Britain, and Italy, the signatory countries of the Memel Statute, against his speech in Nuremberg criticizing Lithuania. Lithuanian Foreign Minister Lozoraitis, currently in Geneva, has been ordered to take the necessary steps. It is reported that Lozoraitis's visit to French Foreign Minister Laval yesterday was related to this matter. Furthermore, the Petit Parisien reported that Laval had advised the Lithuanian Foreign Minister to strictly abide by the Memel Statute and warned him that future Memel elections should be conducted in an orderly manner to avoid unexpected incidents that could lead to serious developments in Eastern Europe. Laval also discussed the Memel issue with Eden. The diplomatic correspondent of the Echo de Paris stated that the Memel issue would not be brought before the League of Nations. (National Telegram, 20th)

Takeshita Returns to Tianjin to Continue Discussing Bandit Suppression Along the Great Wall; Bandits Raid Villages Near the Eastern Tombs at Huanghuashan 57

(Tianjin) The joint Sino-Japanese effort to suppress bandits along the Great Wall is still facing unresolved issues. Takeshita returned to Tianjin early on the 20th after seeking instructions from Changchun. He is scheduled to meet with Chief of Staff Sakai, Staff Officer Nakai, and infantry battalion commanders Kayashima and Onii at the Tokiwa Inn in the Japanese concession in the evening to discuss matters with Yin Rugeng. (Special Dispatch, 20th)

(Tianjin) On the 18th, about 500 bandits with complete firearms and wearing gray uniforms were discovered near Hanmukou in Shanhaiguan. They planned to enter Taitai Touying. The local militia had already dug trenches for defense. The Second Company of the Security Team went to intercept them on the 19th. Bandits entrenched in Huanghuashan, located at the junction of Zunhua and Qian'an, were attacked by Zhang Qingyu's troops on the 18th. Over ten bandits were killed in battle, and the bandit leader Yang Er was seriously wounded and carried away by his accomplices. Villages along the Xinglong-Malan Pass and near the Eastern Tombs were all looted. Residents are fleeing to Malanyu. Although the crops are ripe, they cannot be harvested because the bandits are entrenched in the tall sorghum fields and are abandoned in the wilderness. (Special Dispatch, 20th)

Xiao's Bandits Trapped in Encirclement 58

(Changsha) The 34th Division Commander Gu Jiaqi telegraphed that Xiao's bandits were heavily defeated at Ci Yantang on the 18th. The bandits suffered heavy losses and fled to Zhaotouzhai, where they are now trapped in an encirclement. Defenses in the Longshan-Laifeng area have been further strengthened. (Special Dispatch, 20th)

Harbin's Market is Depressed; Puppet Fleet Forms River Defense Squadron 59

(Tianjin) A visitor from Harbin reported that after the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway, 60,000 Russians have returned to their country. There are now only about 2,000 left in Harbin, which directly affects Chinese and foreign businesses. Shops set up by White Russians have especially little business. The number of Japanese residents has recently increased to over 25,000, and many new shops have been opened, but they cannot revive the depressed market. Chinese merchants are even more unable to close down due to the dumping and oppression of Japanese merchants. They are only trying their best to struggle, seeking to tighten their belts. White Russians are losing their jobs and are living lavishly, many of them going to Shanghai and Tianjin to seek a living. It is rumored that part of the Soviet Amur River defense fleet has been added and has arrived outside the Sanjiang Estuary. The puppet River Defense Fleet has formed two temporary squadrons, with the "Dingyuan" and "Dingbian" ships as the main battleships, commanded by the puppet River Defense Commander Zuo Qian and Japanese advisor Miyakoshi Tatsuki, sailing upstream towards Heihe and Tongjiang on the Heilongjiang River on the 17th to guard against them. (Special Dispatch, 20th)

(Zhenjiang) The Jiangsu Provincial Government Committee resolved on the 20th: 1. Song Mingxin, the chief of the Public Security Bureau, is awarded a major citation of merit. Other personnel who have contributed to the matter will also be rewarded and commended separately to encourage them. 2. The measures for clearing public properties in various counties were approved. 3. In the first phase of the reported allocation of lake fields, for all households holding legal deeds, if the deadline for registering lake fields with grain has passed and they have not yet registered, they will be granted an extension of three months from the date of the registration deadline to complete the registration. If they still fail to register after the extension, the county will implement compulsory registration. (Central News Agency, 20th)

Judicial Yuan Clarifies Ambiguity in Occupying Burial Grounds 65

(Nanjing) Hechuan County, Sichuan, requested an interpretation of how to punish the crime of occupying other people's burial grounds. The Judicial Yuan explained that Article 320, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law clearly stipulates that if one intends to obtain illegal benefits for oneself or a third party, and unlawfully occupies another person's real estate, the situation described in the submission, only occupying and burying on already purchased burial grounds, if it constitutes theft and occupation, can be punished according to the said article. However, attention should be paid to the provisions of Article 1 of the Criminal Law. (Special Dispatch, 20th)
